
THE SONGS OF MALDOROR

by

THE LAUTREAMONT COUNTY




SONGS I, II, III, IV, V, VI




[Drawing: ...; he was dragging his slabs across the room
skin turned]

[Illustration: manuscript of a letter.]



_ To my friend_ ALBERT LACROIX.


The current edition of _Chants de Maldoror_ is a reprint, revised
and corrected from the original manuscript, from a work that never
published in bookstores. In the course of 1869, the Count of Lautréamont
had just issued the last vouchers from his book, and this one
was going to be stapled, when the publisher - continually exposed to
persecutions of the Empire - suspended their sale due to
certain types of violence which made publication dangerous.
"I had a work of poetry published by M. Lacroix. But, once
that it was printed, he refused to publish it, because life
was painted there in colors that were too bitter, and that he feared the
Attorney General."

Thus expresses the author in the letter reproduced in _fac-simile_ in
head of this volume. The poetry work in question and which,
thus presented, attests to the lyrical aim attached by the author, is
well this one. M. le Comte de Lautréamont refused to amend the
violence of his text. It was only after long defending it
that he consented to the modifications which were requested of him. Cartons
intended to replace passages deemed dangerous were to be fired.
But in 1870, war broke out. We no longer thought of the _Chants of
Maldoror_. And suddenly the author died, having executed only one
part of the revisions to which he had consented.

The text of this edition is therefore consistent with that of the edition
original whose print went astray in the cellars of a bookseller
Belgian who timidly after four years broached
copies with anonymous title and cover [1]. A few
literate only know these copies.

We believed that the reissue of such an interesting work would be
well received. His vehemence of style cannot scare an era
as literary as ours. However outraged they are, they keep
of deep beauty and are not pornographic in nature.

Critics will appreciate, as appropriate, the _Chants of Maldoror_,
strange and unequal poem in which, in a furious disorder, collide
admirable episodes and others often confused. By writing this
notice, we just want to destroy a formed legend, we don't know
too much why, with regard to the personality of Count de Lautréamont.
Just recently, Mr. Léon Bloy, whose mission, below, consists
decidedly to demolish everyone, the dead as the living, was trying
to accredit this legend in a long study devoted to volume [2]:
he repeats over and over that the author was mad and that he died mad.
- "It is an insane who speaks, the most deplorable, the most heartbreaking
of the insane. "-" The catastrophe which made this stranger an insane ... "
- "... Because he is a real madman, alas! A real madman who feels his madness. ”
And further: "_The author died in a shed, and that's all we
know about him_. " In writing this, Mr. Léon Bloy knowingly did very
bad job; indeed, it follows from the very thorough investigation that
we did it results from authentic documents that we have
collected, that the author of _Chants de Maldoror_ did not die mad. The
Comte de Lautréamont died at the age of twenty, carried away in two
days with malignant fever. If Mr. Léon Bloy had read the alienists,
and if physiological science had nursed him a little, he would have brought
more reserve in the invention of a fable, interesting only in
point of view of the literary effect he wanted to produce. Science,
indeed, we learn that cases of real madness are extremely rare
below twenty years. However, the author was born in Montevideo on April 4
1850; his manuscript was delivered to the printing press in 1868; we can without
temerity presume its complete completion in 1867; the _Chants of
Maldoror_ therefore emerged from the imagination and cerebral labor of a
young man of seventeen. In addition, the extract of the minutes of the acts
of the ninth arrondissement of Paris wears that Isidore-Lucien
Ducasse - his real name - died on Thursday, November 24
1870, at eight in the morning, at his home, Faubourg-Montmartre, no 7.
The number 7 of Faubourg-Montmartre has never been either a shed or a
crazy's house.

Our active investigations have not resulted in penetrating into its
completeness, the mystery which seems to have been the life of the author in Paris
surrounded. The Prefecture of Police refused to assist us in these
searches, because we had no official character for them
to ask him. This, of course, is a strong administrative rigor
regrettable. What disadvantage can there be in providing an editor
some information on the life of a man of letters dead since
twenty years? Limited to our investigations alone, we have acquired the certainty
that Ducasse had come to Paris in order to attend the courses of
Polytechnic or Mines school. In 1867 he occupied a room
in a hotel located at number 23 rue Notre-Dame-des-Victoires.
He had stayed there as soon as he arrived from America. He was a tall boy
man, brown, beardless, nervous, tidy and hardworking. He only wrote
at night, sitting at his piano. He declaimed, he forged his sentences,
plating his prosopopoeias with chords. This method of composition
made the hotel tenants desperate, who often woke up
startled, could only suspect that an astonishing musician of the verb, a
rare symphonist of the phrase sought, by hitting his keyboard, the
rhythms of his literary orchestration.

If such short cuts in a man’s life are not enough to
reconstruct a very definite resemblance, they will however help
to elucidate, for a small part, the mystery of this figure dedicated to
remain, by almost all sides, obscure. But, restore a character
with documents, doesn't that have something to do with science
occult? At least, have we sought to shed light on this summary portrait
using that of the sciences of that time which, according to a text,
applies to evoke the most fleeting directions of the Soul and the
Thought. Since we had this fortune of having manuscripts of
Ducasse, it seemed curious to ask a learned graphologist his
opinion on the author of _Chants of Maldoror_.

"--Oh! Oh! it's pretty, he says (that's a familiar expression to
graphologists when the subject seems interesting to them); singular
mixture, for example. So see the order and the elegance, this date
regular at the top, this margin, these rigid lines, and this distraction
unexpected which makes him start his letter backwards forgetting the
initials that the paper carries [3] ... Uppercase harmonics: the V of
Voltaire and the R of Rousseau and others. Then look now
_the childishness_ of P de Paris and G of Grandes Têtes. About the
signature, it is literally from a child; how to reconcile
the harmony of such a parafe with what I have just said? We will
have the explanation by analyzing it. He signed: J. Ducasse, without
parafe, he was never to do it, which, you know, is one of the
graphological signs of distinction. Then, remembering that he
was asking for money, he added his address, and to reunite the two
things, by order and logic, he surrounded the whole with a very vague
ellipse made a little "go as I push you" and that it should not
confuse, in this analysis, with the usual spiral parafe
lover of family life. I repeat, there is no
parafe, and _there can not be_, given _the sobriety of the
rest_.

"But, let's continue: harmony showed me an artist, and suddenly I
discovers a logician and a mathematician. The last words: "_the kindness
to write it to me_ ", doesn't that sound like an algebraic formula,
with the abbreviation of _bonté_, and a syllogism, with this narrow
chain of words; and, it is so narrow, this sequence, the
writer is so obsessed with logic that he never puts them
apostrophes only after the finished word, and without forgetting a single one! This is
admirable, maybe I haven't seen this ten times out of the thousands of
letters that I studied.

"Scrupulous and energetic bars with, sometimes, a small harpoon
of selfishness (but who has none?). There is just _ the dose needed_
so as not to alter in any way the kindness which bursts out in the roundness of the letters:
as there is a little prussic acid in almonds, if you will.
A small detail: your man seems a little sensual, there are sometimes
impasto; I'm not angry about this little spot (if it is
a), because really it was too good.

"I sum up: above all, balance: harmony or logic: perhaps
did he never do anything, but I doubt it, because writing is nothing like
lazy: if he's an artist, he might as well have made a
scholar: if he is a scholar, he could just as easily have been a great
artist.

"But is he not mad then?"

"--What do you mean? Or all of the above is true, and everything
it hardly seems crazy to me, or there is no graphology. ”

Only then did we decide to deliver the
some details of Ducasse's life that we know and that,
voluntarily, we had delayed communicating to him for fear of
influence it. And above all, we insisted on this madness that we
reproached and by which one seemed to want to attenuate the conscience
of his talent.

"But I am surprised that such a legend has found credit with
distinguished spirits; you are aware of how much madness at this
are rare, I hear real madness, because idiots,
morons, melancholy, morons, asylums are crowded, but
a real _fou_, a fool of twenty years who, of his madness, would die in a
shed, I doubt that we often see it: even note that this sad detail
and topically, death in a shed immediately reminds me of a
general paralytic with all this classic succession: intelligence
vivid, - obscuration, - madness of persecutions .-- megalomania,
- excitement then complete forfeiture and disappearance of the individual
going for a long time in shreds. Well, question
specialists and ask them how many paralytics they could have
generous of twenty years! Bayle says he has never seen one before
twenty five years; Calmeil only observed it twice before thirty-two
years. Finally, there is mania and circular madness, but these two forms
of insanity follow pretty much the same laws and with infinite exceptions
rare, there is no madman of nineteen years. Finally, if the volume
appeared when Ducasse was nineteen, and died at twenty
years, so this is an alienation that would have evolved in a year ...
not to say with Verlaine: All this is literature! ”

Although Montévidéen, Ducasse was French by origin. His father,
chancellor of the French legation in Montevideo, was born in Tarbes. The
family must have been wealthy. She was in business relationships with
a rue de Lille banker, Mr. Darasse, who paid the son a
monthly pension. Thanks to the kindness of Mr. Dosseur, successor of Mr.
Darasse, we got to know part of the
correspondence of the young writer and give, at the head of this volume,
one of his letters in _fac-simile_. This letter contains in some
so a literary profession of faith and alludes to
circumstances that precluded the sale of his book, as well
as the preface to a new volume, which the publisher Lemerre never
received. Ducasse's correspondence is curious and shows how much
his literary concerns were keen.

In a letter, dated May 22, 1869, we note the passages
following, which we reproduce only as a curiosity:


   "Sir,

   “It was yesterday that I received your letter dated May 21; it was
   yours. Well, know that unfortunately I cannot leave
   so pass the opportunity to express my apologies. Here's why:
   because, if you had announced me the other day, in the ignorance of
   which can be annoying in the circumstances where my person is
   placed, that the funds were running out, I would have been careful not to touch it;
   but certainly I would have felt so much joy in not writing these
   three letters that you would have experienced yourself not to read them.
   You have put into effect the deplorable system of mistrust prescribed
   vaguely by the oddity of my father; but you guessed that
   my headache doesn't stop me from carefully considering the
   difficult situation where you have placed so far a sheet of paper
   letter from South America, the main defect of which was
   lack of clarity; because I do not take into account the
   misunderstanding of some melancholy observations that we forgive
   easily to an old man, and which seemed to me, at first reading,
   to have seemed to impose on you, in the future, perhaps, the necessity
   to step out of your strict role as a banker, vis-à-vis a gentleman
   who comes to live in the capital ...

   "... Sorry, sir, I have a prayer for you: if my father
   sent other funds before September 1, when my
   body will make an appearance in front of your bank door you'll
   kindly let me know? Besides, I'm at home at all
   time of day; but you'd just have to write me a word, and it's
   likely then I will receive it almost as soon as the lady
   who pulls the cord, or well before, if I meet on the
   hallway ...

   "... And all this, I repeat, for an insignificant trifle
   of formality! Present ten dry nails instead of five, the beautiful
   affair: after thinking a lot, I confess that it seemed to me
   filled with a significant amount of zero importance ... "


The author's extreme youth will no doubt attenuate the severity of
some judgments that are sure to be made on the _Chants
from Maldoror_. If Ducasse had lived, he could have become one of the glories
literary of France. He died too soon, leaving behind
his work scattered across the four winds: and by a curious coincidence,
his mortal remains suffered the same fate as his book. Buried in a
temporary concession of the cemetery of the North, on November 25, 1870, it
was exhumed on January 20, 1871 to be re-buried in another
temporary concession. It is currently in the fields
disused and taken over by the City.

LG

--Maldoror - by - the count of Lautréamont - (Songs I, II, III, IV, V, VI)
--Paris and Brussels - On sale at all bookstores - 1874_. Below
of the cover, in the double net, this mention: _All rights of
translation and reproduction reserved_. On the back of the half title:
_Brussels - Typ. by E. Wittmann_. This last indication is false,
no printer by the name of Wittmann having existed in Brussels. Blanket
Brown Brown.

In 1869, the author expressed the desire to have a few copies
from his book; we spit a dozen. The coverage of these
copies is yellow. She wears: _Paris. On sale at all
booksellers (1869) _. On the back of the half title and on the fourth page of the
cover: _Brussels. Printing works by A. Lacroix, Verboeckhoven et Cie,
boulevard de Waterloo, 42_.

[2] _V. la Plume_, 2nd year, no 33.

[3] Photoengraving restored the figure to its place. This one is found
on the fourth page of the letter, crossed out with a stroke of the pen.




THE SONGS OF MALDOROR




SONG FIRST


Would to heaven that the reader, emboldened and momentarily ferocious
like what he reads, finds, without being disoriented, his steep path and
wild, through the desolate swamps of these dark and full pages
poison; because, unless he brings in his reading a logic
rigorous and a tension of spirit equal at least to his distrust, the
deadly fumes from this book will soak his soul like water
sugar. It is not good for everyone to read the pages that go
to follow; only a few will enjoy this bitter fruit safely. By
therefore, shy soul, before penetrating further into such
unexplored moors, direct your heels back and not forward. Listen
well what I tell you: direct your heels backwards and not forward,
like the eyes of a son who respectfully turns away from
august contemplation of the maternal face; or, rather, as an angle
as far as the eye can see, cold cranes meditating a lot, which during
winter, fly powerfully through silence, all sails set,
towards a determined point on the horizon, from which suddenly a wind starts
strange and strong, forerunner of the storm. The oldest crane and
who alone forms the vanguard, seeing this, shakes his head like
a reasonable person, consequently its beak also that it makes
slam, and is not happy (me, either, I would not be
his place), while his old neck, stripped of feathers and contemporary
of three generations of cranes, stirs in irritated ripples which
portend the storm which is approaching more and more. After having
composure looked at several times from all sides with eyes that
contain the experience, carefully, the first (because, it is she who
has the privilege of showing the tail feathers to other cranes
lower in intelligence), with its vigilant cry of melancholy
sentry, to repel the common enemy, it veers with flexibility
the tip of the geometric figure (maybe it's a triangle, but
we don't see the third side that these curious people form in space
passing birds), either to port or to starboard, like a skilful
captain; and, maneuvering with wings that appear no more
as large as a sparrow, because she is not stupid, she
thus takes another philosophical and safer path.

       * * * * *

Reader, maybe this is the hate you want me to invoke in the
beginning of this work! Who says you won't sniff it,
bathed in innumerable pleasures, as long as you like, with your
proud, wide and thin nostrils, tipping your stomach,
like a shark, in the beautiful and black air, as if you understood
the importance of this act and the no less importance of your appetite
legitimate, slowly and majestically, the red emanations? I
assure you, they will delight the two shapeless holes of your hideous snout,
O monster, if you apply yourself before to breathe three thousand
time after time the cursed conscience of the Lord! Your nostrils, which
will be disproportionately dilated with ineffable contentment, ecstasy
still, won't ask for something better from space,
become embalmed like perfumes and incense; because, they will
satiated with complete happiness, like the angels who dwell in the
magnificence and peace of the pleasant skies.

       * * * * *

I will establish in a few lines how Maldoror was good during his
early years, where he lived happily; it is done. Then he saw
that he was born wicked: extraordinary fatality! He hid his character
as long as he could, for a large number of years; but, in the end, at
because of this unnatural concentration every day
blood rushed to his head; until, no longer able to bear
such a life, he threw himself resolutely into the career of evil ...
sweet atmosphere!

       * * * * *

Who would have said it! when he kissed a small child, in the face
pink, he wanted to take his cheeks off with a razor, and he
would have done it very often, if Justice, with its long procession of
punishments, would not have prevented each time. He was not
a liar, he admitted the truth and said he was cruel. Humans,
did you hear? he dares to say it again with this quivering feather!
So therefore, it is a power stronger than the will ...
Curse! The stone would like to evade the laws of
gravity? Impossible. Impossible, if evil wanted to ally with
good. This is what I said above.

       * * * * *

There are some who write to seek human applause,
means of noble qualities of the heart that the imagination invents or that they
can have. I use my genius to paint the delights of
cruelty! Non-transient, artificial delights; but who started
with man, will end up with him. Can't genius ally with
cruelty in the secret resolutions of Providence? or, because
that one is cruel, can't one have genius? We will see the proof
in my words; it's up to you to listen to me, if you want
well ... sorry, it seemed to me that my hair stood on end
head; but, it's nothing, because, with my hand, I managed easily
to put them back in their first position. No one who sings pretends
not that his cavatines are an unknown thing; on the contrary, it
praise that the haughty and wicked thoughts of his hero are
in all men.

       * * * * *

I have seen, throughout my life, without exception of a single one, men, with
narrow shoulders, doing stupid and numerous acts, dumbing down their
alike, and pervert souls by all means. They call them
motives for their actions: glory. Seeing these shows, I wanted
laugh like the others; but this, a strange imitation, was impossible.
I took a penknife whose blade had a sharp edge, and I
split the flesh where the lips meet. One moment I
believed my goal achieved. I looked in a mirror at this bruised mouth
by my own will! It was a mistake! The blood that flowed with
abundance of the two wounds made it difficult to distinguish whether
that was the laughter of others. But after a few moments
comparison, I can see that my laughter was not like that of
human, that is to say that I did not laugh. I saw the men at the head
ugly and with terrible eyes sunk in the dark orbit, surpass
the hardness of the rock, the rigidity of the molten steel, the cruelty of the shark,
the insolence of youth, the senseless fury of criminals, the
betrayals of the hypocrite, the most extraordinary comedians, the
power of character of priests, and the most hidden beings in the
outside, the coldest of worlds and of the sky; tire the moralists
to uncover their hearts, and bring relentless anger upon them
from the top. I saw them all at once, sometimes the strongest fist
directed towards the sky, like that of a child already perverse against his
mother, probably excited by some spirit of hell, eyes
charged with remorse baking at the same time as hateful, in silence
freezing, daring to emit the vast and ungrateful meditations that concealed
their bosom, so full of injustice and horror, and
grieve with compassion the God of mercy; sometimes at every moment
of the day, from the beginning of childhood until the end of
old age, spreading incredible anathemas, which did not have the
common sense, against all that breathes, against themselves and against
Providence, prostitute women and children, and dishonor them
the parts of the body devoted to modesty. So the seas raise
their waters engulf the planks in their abysses; hurricanes,
earthquakes overturn houses; plague, diseases
various decimate the praying families. But, men do not
not see. I saw them also blushing, turning pale with shame for
their conduct on this earth; rarely. Storms, hurricane sisters;
bluish firmament, whose beauty I do not admit; hypocritical sea, picture
from my heart; earth, in a mysterious womb; inhabitants of the spheres; universe
whole; God, who created it magnificently, I am invoking you:
show me a good man! ... But let your grace increase my
natural forces; because at the sight of this monster, I can die
astonishment: you die unless.

             * * * * *

You have to let your nails grow for fifteen days. Oh! like him
is sweet to brutally tear a child who has nothing yet out of bed
on the upper lip, and, with the eyes very open, to make
pretending to smoothly pass his hand over his forehead, tilting
back her beautiful hair! Then suddenly, when he expects it
the least, to push the long nails into his soft chest, so
let him not die; because if he died, we would not have the appearance later
of his miseries. Then we drink the blood by licking the wounds; and,
meanwhile, which should last as long as eternity lasts, the child
cry. Nothing is so good as his blood, extracted as I just said,
and still warm, if not her tears, bitter like salt.
Man, have you never tasted your blood, when by chance you cut yourself
finger? How good it is, isn't it; because, it has no taste. In
Besides, don't you remember having a day in your reflections
dismal, carried by hand, hollowed out at the bottom, on your sickly wet figure
by what fell from the eyes; which hand then fatally headed
towards the mouth, which drew with long lines, in this cup, trembling
like the teeth of the student who looks obliquely at the one born for
oppress her, tears? How good they are, isn't it; because they
taste like vinegar. It looks like the tears of the one who loves the most;
but, the child's tears are better on the palate. He does not betray
not, not yet knowing evil: the one who loves the most betrays early
or late ... I guess by analogy, although I don't know what it is
friendship, than love (it is likely that I will never accept them;
at least on the part of the human race). So since your blood and your
tears don't disgust you, feed yourself, feed yourself with confidence
the teenager's tears and blood. Blindfold him while you
will tear his palpitating flesh; and after hearing long
hours its sublime cries, similar to the piercing groans that grow in
a battle the throats of the dying wounded, then, having pushed you aside
like an avalanche, you will rush from the next room, and you will
pretending to come to his rescue. You will untie her hands, her nerves
and with swollen veins, you will restore sight to his lost eyes,
putting back to licking her tears and her blood. As then repentance is
true! The divine spark which is in us, and appears so rarely, is
watch; too late! How the heart overflows to be able to console the innocent
who were harmed: "Adolescent, who has just suffered from
cruel pains, who therefore could commit a crime on you that I do not
know what name to qualify! Unhappy you are! As you must
suffer! And if your mother knew that, she wouldn't be any closer to
death, so abhorred by the culprits, that I am not now.
Alas! what is good and evil? Is it the same thing by
which we testify with rage our helplessness, and passion
to reach infinity by even the most foolish means? Or,
are these two different things? Yes ... that it is rather the same
thing ... because, if not, what will become of me on the day of judgment! Teenager,
forgive me; it is the one who is before your noble and sacred figure, who
broke your bones and tore the flesh hanging in different places
of your body. Is it a delirium of my sick reason, is it an instinct
secret that does not depend on my reasoning, like that of the eagle
ripping apart its prey, which drove me to commit this crime; and yet
as much as my victim, I suffered! Teenager, forgive me. Once
come out of this fleeting life, I want us to be intertwined
during eternity; form one being, my mouth glued to your
mouth. Even, in this way, my punishment will not be complete. So,
you will tear me, without ever stopping, with teeth and nails
at a time. I will adorn my body with balmy garlands, for this
expiatory holocaust; and we will both suffer from being
torn you to tear me ... my mouth stuck to your mouth. O
teenager, with blond hair, with eyes so sweet, will you do now what
that I advise you? In spite of you, I want you to do it, and you will return
happy my conscience. " After speaking like this, at the same time you will have
hurts a human being, and you will be loved by the same being: this is the
greatest happiness that one can imagine. Later you can
put him in the hospital; because, the perclus will not be able to earn a living. We
will call you good, and laurel wreaths and gold medals
hide your bare feet, scattered on the big tomb, with an old face,
O you, whose name I don't want to write on this page which dedicates the
holiness of crime, I know that your forgiveness was immense like the universe.
But, I still exist!

       * * * * *

I made a pact with prostitution to make a mess
in families. I remember the night before this
dangerous bond. I saw before me a tomb. I heard a
glowworm, big like a house, who says to me: "I will
enlighten you. Read the inscription. It is not from me that this
supreme order. " A vast blood-colored light, looking like
which my jaws snapped and my arms fell inert,
spread through the air to the horizon. I leaned against
a ruined wall, for I was about to fall, and I read: "Here is a
teenager who died of breast cancer: you know why. Don't pray
not for him. " Many men may not have had
as much courage as me. Meanwhile, a beautiful naked woman
came to lie down at my feet. Me, hers, with a sad figure:
"You can get up." I held out my hand with which the
fratricide slays his sister's throat. The glow worm, to me: "You, take
a stone and kill it; - Why? I said." Him, to me: "Take
beware; the weakest, because I am the strongest.
This is called _Prostitution_. " Tears in my eyes,
rage in the heart, I felt an unknown force being born in me.
I took a large stone; after much effort, I raised it
with difficulty to the height of my chest; I put it on
the shoulder with the arms. I climb a mountain to the top:
from there I crushed the glow-worm. His head sank under the ground
greatness of a man; the stone bounces up to the height of
six churches. She went back to a lake, whose waters
lowered for a moment, spinning, digging a huge
inverted cone. Calm reappeared on the surface; blood light
no longer shone. "Alas! Alas! cried the beautiful naked woman;
what did you do?" Me, to her: “I prefer you to him; because I have
pity the unhappy. It's not your fault, if justice
eternal created you. " She, to me: "One day, men
will do justice; I don't tell you more. Leave me
leave to hide my infinite sadness at the bottom of the sea.
Only you and the hideous monsters swarm in these
black abysses, which do not despise me. You are good. Goodbye, you who
loved me! ” Me, to her: “Farewell! Again: farewell! I
will always love you! ... As of today, I give up virtue. "
This is why, O people, when you hear the winter wind
groaning on the sea and near its edges, or above large
cities that have long mourned for me, or
across the cold polar regions, say, "It's not
the spirit of God passing by: this is only the sharp sigh of the
prostitution, united with the serious groans of the Montevideen. "
Children, I'm telling you this. So, full of mercy,
kneel down; and that men, more numerous than lice,
make long prayers.

       * * * * *

In the moonlight, near the sea, in remote areas of the
countryside, we see, immersed in bitter reflections, all things
put on yellow, indecisive, fantastic shapes. The shade of the trees,
sometimes fast, sometimes slowly, short, come, come back, by various
shapes, flattening, sticking against the ground. In time,
when I was carried on the wings of youth, it made me
dreaming, seemed strange to me; now I'm used to it. Wind
groans through the leaves its languorous notes, and the owl sings
his grave lament, which makes the hair of those who hear it stand up.
So the dogs, made furious, break their chains, escape from
distant farms; they run in the countryside, here and there, plagued by
madness. Suddenly they stop, look from all sides with a
wild anxiety, the eye on fire; and, like the elephants, before
to die, take a last look at the sky in the desert, raising
desperately cheats on them, leaving their ears inert, so too
dogs leave their ears inert, raise their head, swell their neck
terrible, and begin to bark, in turn, like a child who
screams of hunger, like a wounded cat in the stomach above a roof,
either as a woman who is going to give birth, or as a dying man with
the plague in the hospital, like a young girl singing a sublime tune,
against the stars in the north, against the stars in the east, against the stars
to the south, against the stars to the west; against the moon; against the mountains,
distant like giant rocks, lying in the dark; against
the cold air they breathe in, making the inside of their
nostril, red, burning; against the silence of the night; against owls,
whose oblique flight shaves their snout, carrying a rat or a frog
in the beak, live food, sweet for the little ones; against hares,
which disappear in the blink of an eye; against the thief, who fled to
galloping his horse after committing a crime; against snakes,
stirring the heather, which makes them tremble the skin, gnash their teeth;
against their own barking, which scares them to themselves; against the
toads they grind with one jaw (why did they
far from the marsh?); against the trees, whose leaves, limply
rocked, are as many mysteries that they do not understand, that they want
discover with their fixed, intelligent eyes; against spiders,
suspended between their long legs, which climb trees to get
to save; against crows who did not find something to eat during the
day, and who return to the lodge the tired wing; against the rocks
from the shore; against fires, which appear on the masts of invisible ships;
against the dull sound of the waves; against the big fish, which, swimming,
show their black backs, then sink into the abyss; and against man
which makes them slaves. After which, they start running again
the countryside, leaping, with their bloody legs, over the ditches,
paths, fields, grasses and steep stones. They look like
rabies, seeking a large pond to quench their thirst. Their
prolonged howls terrify nature. Woe to the lingering traveler!
Friends of cemeteries will throw themselves on him, tear him apart, eat him,
with their mouth from which blood falls; because, they do not have spoiled teeth.
Wild animals, not daring to approach to take part in the meal
of flesh, run away as far as the eye can see, trembling. After a few hours, the
dogs, exhausted from running here and there, almost dead, their tongues outside
mouth, rush on each other, without knowing what they
do, and tear into a thousand shreds, with incredible speed. They
do not do so out of cruelty. One day, with glassy eyes, my mother
said to me: "When you are in your bed, you will hear the barking
dogs in the countryside, hide in your blanket, don't turn
make fun of what they do: they have an insatiable thirst for the infinite, like you,
like me, like the rest of humans, with a pale, long face. Same,
I allow you to stand in front of the window to contemplate this spectacle,
which is quite sublime. " Since that time, I respect the wish of the dead.
I, like dogs, feel the need for infinity ... I cannot, I
can not satisfy this need! I am the son of man and woman,
from what I was told. It surprises me ... I thought I was more! At
rest, what does it matter to me where i come from? Me, if it could have depended on my
will, I would rather have been the son of the female shark, whose
hunger is friend of storms, and of the tiger, with recognized cruelty: I do not
wouldn't be so mean. You who look at me, move away from me, because
my breath exhales a poisoned breath. No one has seen wrinkles yet
green on my forehead; nor the protruding bones of my thin figure, like
ridges of some large fish, or rocks covering the shores of the
sea, or to the steep alpine mountains, which I often crossed, when
I had hair of another color on my head. And when I roam
around men's homes, during stormy nights, eyes
fiery, hair flogged by the wind of storms, isolated like a
stone in the middle of the path, I cover my withered face, with a piece
of velvet, black like the soot that fills the interior of the chimneys: it
the eyes must not witness the ugliness that the Supreme Being,
with a smile of powerful hatred, put on me. Every morning when
the sun rises for others, spreading joy and warmth
beneficial in nature, while none of my features move,
staring at the space full of darkness, crouching towards the bottom of
my beloved cave, in a despair that intoxicates me like wine, I bruise
with my mighty hands my tattered chest. However, I feel that I
don't get rabies! However, I feel that I am not the
alone who suffers! However, I feel that I breathe! Like a convict who
try his muscles, thinking about their fate, and that will soon
go up to the scaffold, standing on my bed of straw, eyes closed, I
slowly turn my collar from right to left, from left to right, during
whole hours; I don't fall dead. From moment to moment,
when my cervix can no longer continue to turn in the same direction, it
stop, to start turning in an opposite direction, I look
suddenly the horizon, through the rare interstices left by
thick brush covering the entrance: I can't see anything! Nothing ...
if not the countryside dancing in swirls with the trees and
with long lines of birds crossing the air. It troubles me
the blood and the brain ... Who then, on the head, kicks me
iron bar, like a hammer striking the anvil?

       * * * * *

I propose, without being moved, to declaim aloud the stanza
serious and cold that you will hear. You pay attention to
what it contains, and beware of the painful impression that it does
will not fail to leave, like a wilt, in your imaginations
troubled. Don't think I'm about to die, because I don't
am not yet a skeleton, and old age is not stuck to my
forehead. So let's dismiss any idea of ​​comparison with the swan,
as its existence flies away, and see before you only one
monster, which I am glad you cannot see
figure; but, less horrible is she than her soul. However, I am not
not a criminal ... Enough on this subject. I haven't been long
reviewed the sea, and set foot on the ship deck, and my memories are
perennial as if I had left it the day before. Be nevertheless, if you
as calm as I can, in this reading that I repent of
already to offer you, and don't blush at the thought of what the
human heart. O octopus, with a silk look! you, whose soul is
inseparable from mine; you, the most beautiful of the inhabitants of the globe
terrestrial, and who commands a seraglio of four hundred suction cups; you,
in which sit nobly, as in their natural residence, by a
by mutual agreement, of an indestructible bond, the soft communicative virtue and
divine graces, why are you not with me, your belly of mercury
against my aluminum chest, both sitting on some rock
from the shore, to contemplate this spectacle which I adore!

Old ocean, with crystal waves, you resemble in proportion to
these azure marks that we see on the bruised back of mosses; you
are a huge blue, applied to the body of the earth: I like this
comparison. So, at your first appearance, a prolonged breath of
sadness, that one would believe to be the murmur of your sweet breeze, pass, in
leaving indelible traces on the deeply shaken soul, and
you remember the memories of your lovers, without always being surrendered
account, the rough beginnings of man, where he gets to know
the pain, which never leaves him. I salute you, old ocean!

Old ocean, your harmoniously spherical shape, which delights the face
serious geometry, reminds me only too much of the little eyes of
man, like those of the boar for smallness, and those of
night owls for circular perfection of the outline. However,
man has believed himself handsome in all ages. I rather assume that
man believes in his beauty only by self-love; but, that it is not
really beautiful and he suspects it because, why is he looking at the
figure of his fellow with so much contempt? I salute you, old ocean!

Old ocean, you are the symbol of identity: always equal to yourself.
You do not vary in an essential way, and, if your waves are
somewhere furious, further away, in some other area, they are
in the most complete calm. You are not like the man who stops
in the street, to see two dodds grabbing their necks, but who
does not stop when a funeral passes; which is accessible this morning
and tonight in a bad mood; who laughs today and cries tomorrow. I
greet you, old ocean!

Old ocean, there would be nothing impossible for you to hide in your
within future uses for man. You already gave him the whale.
You don't easily let science-hungry eyes guess
natural the thousand secrets of your intimate organization: you are modest.
The man constantly boasts, and for minutiae. I salute you, old man
ocean!

Old ocean, the different species of fish you feed have
not sworn brotherhood between them. Each species lives on its own. The
temperaments and conformations that vary in each of them,
explain, in a satisfactory manner, what seems at first only a
anomaly. So it is with man, who does not have the same motives
excuse. Is a piece of land occupied by thirty million beings
humans, they believe they are obliged not to interfere in the existence of
their neighbors, fixed like roots on the following piece of land.
Descending from big to small, each man lives like a savage in
his den, and rarely leaves it to visit his fellow, crouching
similarly in another den. The great universal family of
humans is a utopia worthy of the most mediocre logic. In addition,
from the sight of your fertile breasts, the notion of ingratitude emerges;
because we immediately think of these numerous parents, who are quite ungrateful towards the
Creator, to abandon the fruit of their miserable union. I salute you,
old ocean!

Old ocean, your material greatness can only be compared to the measure
that we make of what it took active power to generate the
all of your mass. We can't kiss you at a glance. For
to contemplate you, the sight must turn its telescope, by a movement
continuous, towards the four points of the horizon, as well as a
mathematician, in order to solve an algebraic equation, is forced
to examine the various possible cases separately before deciding the
difficulty. Man eats nourishing substances, and makes others
efforts, worthy of a better fate, to appear fat. That she
swell as much as it likes, this adorable frog. Be quiet,
it won't match you in size; I suppose so, at least. I salute you,
old ocean!

Old ocean, your waters are bitter. It's exactly the same taste as the
gall that criticism distils on the fine arts, on the sciences, on
all. If someone has genius, they pass him off as an idiot; if
some other is beautiful in body, it is a hideous hunchback. Certainly,
let the man strongly feel his imperfection, three-quarters of which
moreover are due only to himself, to criticize it thus! I
salute, old ocean!

Old ocean, men, despite the excellence of their methods, are
not yet reached, helped by the means of investigation of science,
to measure the vertiginous depth of your abysses; you only have them
the longest, heaviest probes recognized that they were inaccessible.
Fish ... it's allowed: not men. I often
asked which thing was easier to recognize: the depth
from the ocean or the depth of the human heart! Often the hand brought to the
forehead standing on the vessels as the moon swayed between
the masts irregularly, I surprised myself, doing
disregarding everything that was not the goal I was pursuing,
m'efforçant de résoudre ce difficile problème! Oui, quel est le plus
profond, le plus impénétrable des deux: l'océan ou le coeur humain?
Si trente ans d'expérience de la vie peuvent jusqu'à un certain point
pencher la balance vers l'une ou l'autre de ces solutions, il me sera
permis de dire que, malgré la profondeur de l'océan, il ne peut pas se
mettre en ligné, quant à la comparaison sur cette propriété, avec la
profondeur du coeur humain. J'ai été en relation avec des hommes qui ont
été vertueux. Ils mouraient à soixante ans, et chacun ne manquait pas de
exclaim: "They have done good on this earth, that is to say, they have
practiced charity: that's all, it's not smart, everyone can
do the same. " Who will understand why two lovers who idolized
the day before, for a misinterpreted word, move away, one towards the east,
the other towards the west, with the stings of hatred, of
revenge, love and remorse, and never see each other again
draped in his lonely pride? It's a miracle that is renewed
every day, which is no less miraculous. Who will understand
why we savor not only the general disgraces of our
similar, but still the particulars of his dearest friends,
while we are afflicted at the same time? An undeniable example
to end the series: the man hypocritically says yes and thinks no. This is
why the wild boars of humanity have so much confidence in one
in others and are not selfish. It remains to psychology
a lot of progress to be made. I salute you, old ocean!

Old ocean, you are so powerful, that men taught it to their
own costs. They may use all the resources of their
genius ... unable to dominate you. They found their master. I say
that they found something stronger than them. This something
has a name. This name is: the ocean! The fear that you inspire in him is such,
that they respect you. Despite this, you are waltzing their heaviest
machines with grace, elegance and ease. You make them jump
gymnastics to the sky, and wonderful dives to the bottom of
your domains: a acrobat would be jealous. Blessed are they,
when you don’t wrap them up in your bubbling folds,
to go and see, without a railway, in your aquatic entrails,
how the fish are doing, and especially how they are doing
themselves. The man says, "I'm smarter than the ocean." This is
possible, it's even quite true; but the ocean is more formidable to him
than him in the ocean: this is not necessary to prove. This
patriarch observer, contemporary of the first eras of our
hanging globe, smiles in pity, when he attends the naval battles of
nations. Here are a hundred leviathans who came out of the hands of
humanity. The emphatic orders of the superiors, the cries of the wounded,
the cannon shots are noise made on purpose to destroy some
seconds. It seems that the drama is over, and that the ocean has put everything
in her womb. The face is great. She must be tall towards
low, in the direction of the unknown! To finally crown the stupid
comedy, which is not even interesting, we see, in the middle of the air,
some stork, retarded by fatigue, who starts to cry, without
stop the scale of his flight: "Here! ... I find it bad! There is
had black dots below; I closed my eyes: they have disappeared. ”
I salute you, old ocean!

Old ocean, oh great bachelor, when you travel solemn solitude
of your phlegmatic realms, you rightly take pride in your
native magnificence, and true praise that I hasten to give you.
Swung voluptuously by the fragrant mols of your majestic slowness,
which is the grandest among the attributes of which sovereign power
gratified you, you unroll, in the middle of a dark mystery, on all your
sublime surface, your incomparable waves, with the calm feeling of your
eternal power. They follow each other in parallel, separated by
short intervals. Barely one decreases, another goes to meet it
growing up, accompanied by the melancholy sound of foam melting,
to warn us that everything is scum. (So ​​human beings, these
living waves, die one after the other, in a monotonous manner; But,
without leaving a frothy noise). The passing bird sits on them
avec confiance, et se laisse abandonner à leurs mouvements, pleins d'une
grâce fière, jusqu'à ce que les os de ses ailes aient recouvré leur vigueur
accoutumée pour continuer leur pèlerinage aérien. Je voudrais que la
majesté humaine ne fût que l'incarnation du reflet de la tienne. Je demande
beaucoup, et ce souhait sincère est glorieux pour toi. Ta grandeur morale,
image de l'infini, est immense comme la réflexion du philosophe, comme
l'amour de la femme, comme la beauté divine de l'oiseau, comme les
méditations du poëte. Tu es plus beau que la nuit. Réponds-moi, océan,
veux-tu être mon frère? Remue-toi avec impétuosité ... plus ... plus
encore, si tu veux que je te compare à la vengeance de Dieu; allonge tes
griffes livides en te frayant un chemin sur ton propre sein ... c'est bien.
Déroule tes vagues épouvantables, océan hideux, compris par moi seul, et
devant lequel je tombe, prosterné à tes genoux. La majesté de l'homme est
empruntée; il ne m'imposera point: toi, oui. Oh! quand tu t'avances, la
high and terrible crest, surrounded by your tortuous folds like a courtyard,
magnetizer and fierce, rolling your waves on top of each other, with
awareness of what you are, as you push, from the depths of
your chest, as if overwhelmed by an intense remorse that I cannot
discover, that muffled perpetual roar that men fear so much,
even when they contemplate you, safe, trembling on the shore,
so I see it doesn't belong to me, the insignificant right to tell me
your equal. This is why, in the presence of your superiority, I would give you
all my love (and no one knows how much love my
aspirations towards the beautiful), if you did not make me painfully think
to my fellows, who form the most ironic contrast with you,
the most clownish antithesis we have ever seen in creation:
I can't love you, I hate you. Why do I come back to you, for
the thousandth time, towards your friendly arms, which part, to caress
my burning forehead, which sees the fever disappear on contact! I do not
don't know your hidden destiny; everything that concerns you interests me.
Tell me then if you are the home of the prince of darkness. Tell me ...
tell me, ocean (to me alone, so as not to sadden those who have
still known as illusions), and if the breath of Satan creates the
storms that lift your salt water to the clouds. You have to
tell me, because I would be glad to know hell so close to
the man. I want this to be the last stanza of my
invocation. Therefore, once again, I want to greet you and
say goodbye to you! Old ocean, with crystal waves ... My eyes are
wet abundant tears, and I do not have the strength to continue;
because, I feel that the time has come to return among men, to the appearance
brutal; but ... courage! Let’s make a big effort, and let’s accomplish,
with the feeling of duty, our destiny on this earth. I
salute, old ocean!

       * * * * *

They won't see me at my last hour (I write this on my bed
dead), surrounded by priests. I want to die, lulled by the sea wave
stormy, or standing on the mountain ... eyes up, no: I
know that my annihilation will be complete. Besides, I would not have
thanks to hope. Who opens the door to my burial chamber? I said
let no one come in. Whoever you are, get away; but, if you
think you see some mark of pain or fear on my face
hyena (I use this comparison, although the hyena is more beautiful than
me, and more pleasant to see), think again: let him approach. We
are in a winter night as the elements collide
everywhere, that the man is afraid, and that the adolescent meditates some
crime on one of his friends, if he was what I was in my youth. that
the wind, whose plaintive whistles sadden humanity, since
that the wind, humanity exists, moments before the agony
last, carry me on the bones of his wings, around the world,
impatient for my death. I will still enjoy, in secret, the examples
many of human wickedness (a brother, without being seen, likes to see
acts of his brothers). The eagle, the raven, the immortal pelican, the
wild duck, traveling crane, awake, shivering with cold, me
will see the lightning flash, horrible and happy specter. They
won't know what it means. On earth, the viper, the big eye of the
toad, tiger, elephant; in the sea, the whale, the shark, the
hammer, the shapeless stripe, the tooth of the polar seal, will wonder
what is this derogation from the law of nature. Man, trembling,
will stick his forehead against the earth, in the midst of his groans. "Yes,
I surpass you all by my innate cruelty, cruelty that it does not have
depended on me to erase. Is it for this reason that you show yourself
before me in this prostration? or is it because you
see it travel, new phenomenon, like a frightening comet,
bloody space? (I am showered with blood from my vast body,
like a blackish cloud pushed by the hurricane in front of you). Don't fear
nothing, children, I don't want to curse you. The harm you have done to me
is too great, too great the harm I have done to you, for it to be
voluntary. You, you have walked in your way, I, in the
mine, both alike, both perverse.
Nécessairement, nous avons dû nous rencontrer, dans cette similitude de
caractère; le choc qui en est résulté nous a été réciproquement fatal.»
Alors, les hommes relèveront peu à peu la tête, en reprenant courage,
pour voir celui qui parle ainsi, allongeant le cou comme l'escargot.
Tout à coup, leur visage brûlant, décomposé, montrant les plus terribles
passions, grimacera de telle manière que les loups auront peur. Ils se
dresseront à la fois comme un ressort immense. Quelles imprécations!
quels déchirements de voix! Ils m'ont reconnu. Voilà que les animaux
de la terre se réunissent aux hommes, font entendre leurs bizarres
clameurs. Plus de haine réciproque; les deux haines sont tournées contre
l'ennemi commun, moi; on se rapproche par un assentiment universel.
Vents, qui me soutenez, élevez-moi plus haut; je crains la perfidie.
Oui, disparaissons peu à peu de leurs yeux, témoin, une fois de plus,
des conséquences des passions, complément satisfait ... Je te remercie,
ô rhinolophe, de m'avoir réveillé avec le mouvement de tes ailes, toi,
dont le nez est surmonté d'une crête en forme de fer à cheval: je
m'aperçois, en effet, que ce n'était malheureusement qu'une maladie
passagère, et je me sens avec dégoût renaître à la vie. Les uns disent
que tu arrivais vers moi pour me sucer le peu de sang qui se trouve dans
mon corps: pourquoi cette hypothèse n'est-elle pas la réalité!

       *       *       *       *       *

Une famille entoure une lampe posée sur la table:

--Mon fils, donne-moi les ciseaux qui sont placés sur cette chaise.

--Ils n'y sont pas, mère.

--Va les chercher alors dans l'autre chambre. Te rappelles-tu cette
époque, mon doux maître, où nous faisions des voeux, pour avoir un
enfant, dans lequel nous renaîtrions une seconde fois, et qui serait le
support of our old age?

--I remember it, and God heard us. We don't have to
complain about our lot on this earth. Every day we bless the
Providence of its benefits. Our Edward has all the graces of
his mother.

--And the male qualities of his father.

--Here are the scissors, mother; I finally found them.

He goes back to work ... But someone showed up at the door
entry, and contemplate, for a few moments, the table which
offers to him:

--What does this show mean! There are a lot of people who are less
happy that those. What is the reasoning they do to love
existence? Get away, Maldoror, from this peaceful home; your place is
not here.

He retired!

--I do not know how it is done; but, I feel the human faculties
who are fighting in my heart. My soul is worried, and without
know why; the atmosphere is heavy.

--Woman, I feel the same impressions as you; I tremble that he does
some misfortune happens to us. Let us trust in God; in him is the
supreme hope.

--Mother, I hardly breathe: my head hurts.

--You too my son! I'm going to wet your forehead and temples with
vinegar.

--No, good mother ...

See, he's leaning his body on the back of the chair, tired.

--Something is going back inside me, which I cannot explain.
Now the slightest object annoys me.

- How pale you are! The end of this vigil will not happen without
some fatal event plunges the three of us into the
despair!

I hear, in the distance, prolonged cries of the most pain
poignant.

--My son!

--Ah! mother! ... I'm afraid!

--Tell me quickly if you suffer.

--Mother, I am not suffering ... I am not telling the truth.

The father does not return from his astonishment:

--These are the cries that we sometimes hear, in the silence of the nights
without stars. Although we hear these cries, however, whoever
sprout is not near here; because, we can hear these groans at
three leagues away, carried by the wind from a city to a
other. I had often been told about this phenomenon: but, I had never
had the opportunity to judge for myself its veracity. Woman, you were talking to me
of doom; if more real misfortune existed in the long spiral of time,
it is the misfortune of him who now disturbs the sleep of his
similar ...

I hear in the distance cries prolonged from the most pain
poignant.

--Plût au ciel que sa naissance ne soit pas une calamité pour son pays,
qui l'a repoussé de son sein. Il va de contrée en contrée, abhorré
partout. Les uns disent qu'il est accablé d'une espèce de folie
originelle, depuis son enfance. D'autres croient savoir qu'il est d'une
cruauté extrême et instinctive, dont il a honte lui-même, et que ses
parents en sont morts de douleur. Il y en a qui prétendent qu'on l'a
flétri d'un surnom dans sa jeunesse: qu'il en est resté inconsolable le
reste de son existence, parce que sa dignité blessée voyait là une
preuve flagrante de la méchanceté des hommes, qui se montre aux
premières années, pour augmenter ensuite. Ce surnom était _le
vampire_!...

J'entends dans le lointain des cris prolongés de la douleur la plus
poignante.

--They add that, days, nights, without truce or rest,
horrible nightmares make him bleed blood from his mouth and
ears; and specters sit at the bedside, and he
throw in the face, pushed in spite of themselves by an unknown force, sometimes
in a soft voice, sometimes in a voice like the roars of
fights, with relentless persistence, this nickname still alive,
always hideous, and which will only perish with the universe. Some even
claimed that love reduced him to this state: or that these cries
bear witness to the repentance of some crime buried on the night of his
mysterious past. But most people think that an immeasurable
torture, as Satan once did, and he wanted to equal God ...

I hear in the distance cries prolonged from the most pain
poignant.

--My son, these are exceptional secrets: I pity your
age of hearing them, and I hope you will never imitate this
man.

Speak, oh my Edward; answer that you will never imitate this man.

--O beloved mother, to whom I owe the day, I promise you, if the saint
promise of a child has any value, never to imitate this man.

"It is perfect, my son; you have to obey your mother, whatever it is.

We no longer hear the groans.

--Woman, have you finished your work?

--I am missing a few points on this shirt, although we have
extended the day before very late.

- Me too, I haven't finished a chapter started. Let's take advantage of
last lights of the lamp; because there is almost no oil left, and
let's each finish our work ...

The child exclaimed:

--Si Dieu nous laisse vivre!

--Ange radieux, viens à moi: tu te promèneras dans la prairie, du matin
jusqu'au soir: tu ne travailleras point. Mon palais magnifique est
construit avec des murailles d'argent, des colonnes d'or et des portes
de diamants. Tu te coucheras quand tu voudras, au son d'une musique
céleste, sans faire ta prière. Quand, au matin, le soleil montrera ses
rayons resplendissants et que l'alouette joyeuse emportera, avec elle,

jusqu'à ce que cela te fatigue. Tu marcheras sur les tapis les plus
précieux; tu seras constamment enveloppé dans une atmosphère composée

--Il est temps de reposer le corps et l'esprit. Lève-toi, mère de
family, on your muscular ankles. It's just that your fingers
stiffened abandon the needle of exaggerated labor. Extremes have
nothing good.

--Oh! how sweet your existence will be! I will give you an enchanted ring;
when you return the ruby, you will be invisible, like the princes,
in fairy tales.

- Put your daily weapons back in the protective cupboard, while,
on my side, I arrange my business.

--When you put it back in its ordinary position, you will reappear as
that nature has formed you, O young magician. This, because I love you and
that I aspire to make you happy.

- Go away, whoever you are; don't take me by the shoulders.

--My son, do not fall asleep, lulled by the dreams of childhood: the
common prayer is not started and your clothes are not yet
soigneusement placés sur une chaise ... A genoux! Éternel créateur de
l'univers, tu montres la bonté inépuisable jusque dans les plus petites
choses.

--Tu n'aimes donc pas les ruisseaux limpides, où glissent des milliers
de petits poissons rouges, bleus et argentés? Tu les prendras avec un
filet si beau, qu'il les attirera de lui-même, jusqu'à ce qu'il soit
rempli. De la surface, tu verras des cailloux brillants, plus polis que
le marbre.

--Mère, vois ces griffes; je me méfie de lui; mais ma conscience est
calme, car je n'ai rien à me reprocher.

--Tu nous vois, prosternés à tes pieds, accablés du sentiment de ta
grandeur. Si quelque pensée orgueilleuse s'insinue dans notre
imagination, nous la rejetons aussitôt avec la salive du dédain et
nous t'en faisons le sacrifice irrémissible.

--Tu t'y baigneras avec de petites filles, qui t'enlaceront de leurs
bras. Une fois sortis du bain, elles te tresseront des couronnes de
roses et d'oeillets. Elles auront des ailes transparentes de papillon
et des cheveux d'une longueur ondulée, qui flottent autour de la
gentillesse de leur front.

--Quand même ton palais serait plus beau que le cristal, je ne sortirais
pas de cette maison pour te suivre. Je crois que tu n'es qu'un
impostor, since you talk to me so softly, for fear of making you
hear. Abandoning your parents is a bad thing. It's not
I who would be an ungrateful son. As for your little girls, they are not
not as beautiful as my mother's eyes.

--All our lives have been exhausted in the songs of your glory. Such
we have been so far, as we will be, until we
will receive from you the order to leave this earth.

--They will obey you at your slightest sign and will only think of pleasing you.
If you want the bird that never rests, they will bring it to you.
If you want the snow car, which transports to the sun in the blink of an eye
look, they will bring it to you. What would they not bring you! They
would even bring you the kite, tall as a tower, that we hid
in the moon, and at the tail of which are suspended, by links of
silk, birds of all kinds. Pay attention to you ... listen to my
advice.

--Do what you want: I don't want to interrupt my prayer, to
Call for help. Whatever your body evaporates, when I want
dismiss it, know that I do not fear you.

--Front of you, nothing is great, except the flame exhaled from a heart
pure.

--Think about what I told you, if you don't want to repent.

--Heavenly Father, conjure, conjure up the misfortunes that can melt on
our family.

--So you do not want to withdraw, evil spirit?

- Keep this beloved wife, who comforted me in my discouragement
...

--Since you refuse me, I'll make you cry and cringe like
a hanged.

--And this loving son, whose chaste lips barely open to
kisses of the dawn of life.

--Mother, he is strangling me ... Father, rescue me ... I can no longer
breathe ... Your blessing!

A cry of immense irony rose in the air. See how
eagles, dizzy, fall from the clouds, rolling in on themselves,
littéralement foudroyés par la colonne d'air.

--Son coeur ne bat plus ... Et celle-ci est morte, en même temps que le
fruit de ses entrailles, fruit que je ne reconnais plus, tant il est
défiguré ... Mon épouse!... Mon fils!... Je me rappelle un temps
lointain où je fus époux et père.

Il s'était dit, devant le tableau qui s'offrit à ses yeux, qu'il ne
supporterait pas cette injustice. S'il est efficace, le pouvoir que lui
have bestowed infernal spirits, or rather that he draws from himself, this
child, before the night passes, should no longer be.

       * * * * *

The one who does not know how to cry (because he has always repressed suffering
inside) noticed that he was in Norway. In the Faeroé Islands, there
assisted in the search for seabird nests, in crevices
sheer, and was astonished that the three hundred meter rope, which holds
the explorer over the precipice was chosen with such solidity.
He saw there, whatever we say, a striking example of human kindness,
and he couldn't believe his eyes. If he was the one who should have prepared
the rope, he would have made cuts in several places, so
let it cut itself, and throw the hunter into the sea! One evening he
dirigea vers un cimetière, et les adolescents qui trouvent du plaisir à
violer les cadavres de belles femmes mortes depuis peu, purent, s'ils le
voulurent, entendre la conversation suivante, perdue dans le tableau
d'une action qui va se dérouler en même temps.

--N'est-ce pas, fossoyeur, que tu voudras causer avec moi? Un cachalot
s'élève peu à peu du fond de la mer, et montre sa tête au-dessus des
eaux, pour voir le navire qui passe dans ses parages solitaires. La
curiosité naquit avec l'univers.

--Ami, il m'est impossible d'échanger des idées avec toi. Il y a
longtemps que les doux rayons de la lune font briller le marbre des
tombeaux. C'est l'heure silencieuse où plus d'un être humain rêve qu'il
voit apparaître des femmes enchaînées, traînant leurs linceuls, couverts
de taches de sang, comme un ciel noir, d'étoiles. Celui qui dort pousse
des gémissements, pareils à ceux d'un condamné à mort, jusqu'à ce qu'il
se réveille, et s'aperçoive que la réalité est trois fois pire que le
rêve. Je dois finir de creuser cette fosse, avec ma bêche infatigable,
so that it’s ready tomorrow morning. To do serious work, it
don't do two things at once.

--He believes that digging a pit is serious work! You think that
digging a pit is serious work?

--When the wild pelican resolves to give its breast to devour
his little ones, having as witness only the one who knew how to create such a love,
in order to shame men, though the sacrifice is great, this
act is understandable. When a young man sees, in the arms of his friend,
a woman whom he idolized, he then began to smoke a cigar; he ... not
not come out of the house, and form an indissoluble friendship with the
pain; this act is understandable. When an internal student in a high school,
is ruled, for years, which are centuries, from morning
until evening and from evening until the following day, by a pariah of the
civilization, which constantly has its eyes on it, it feels the waves
tumultuous of a perennial hatred, rising like thick smoke, to his
brain, which seems to him to explode. From the moment we threw it away
in the prison, up to the one who approaches, where he will leave, a
intense fever turns his face yellow, brings his eyebrows together, and digs him
the eyes. At night he thinks because he doesn't want to sleep. The
jour, sa pensée s'élance au-dessus des murailles de la demeure de
l'abrutissement, jusqu'au moment où il s'échappe, ou qu'on le rejette,
comme un pestiféré, de ce cloître éternel; cet acte se comprend. Creuser
une fosse dépasse souvent les forces de la nature. Comment veux-tu,
étranger, que la pioche remue cette terre, qui d'abord nous nourrit, et
puis nous donne un lit commode, préservé du vent de l'hiver soufflant
avec furie dans ces froides contrées, lorsque celui qui tient la pioche,
de ses tremblantes mains, après avoir toute la journée palpé
convulsivement les joues des anciens vivants qui rentrent dans son
royaume, voit, le soir, devant lui, écrit en lettres de flammes, sur
chaque croix de bois, l'énoncé du problème effrayant que l'humanité n'a
pas encore résolu: la mortalité ou l'immortalité de l'âme. Le créateur
de l'univers, je lui ai toujours conservé mon amour; mais, si, après la
mort, nous ne devons plus exister, pourquoi vois-je, la plupart des
nuits, chaque tombe s'ouvrir, et leurs habitants soulever doucement les
lead covers, to breathe fresh air?

--Stop in your work. Emotion takes away your strength; you ... me
seem weak like the reed; it would be great folly to continue.
I am strong: I will take your place. You put yourself aside; you ... me
will give advice, if I am not doing well.

--That his arms are muscular, and that there is pleasure in looking at him
dig the earth so easily!

--It must not be that an unnecessary doubt torments your thought: all these
graves, which are scattered in a cemetery, like flowers in a
prairie, comparison that lacks truth, are worth measuring
with the philosopher's serene compass. Dangerous hallucinations
can come during the day; but, they mostly come at night. By
Therefore, do not be surprised by the fantastic visions that your eyes
seem to notice. During the day, when the mind is at rest,
question your conscience; she will tell you, with certainty, that the God who
created man with a plot of his own intelligence has a
kindness without limits, and will receive, after earthly death, this chief-
of work within it. Gravedigger, why are you crying? Why these
tears, like a woman's? Remember the good; we are
on this ship dismasted to suffer. It is a merit for man that
God judged him capable of overcoming his most serious sufferings.
Speak, and since, according to your dearest wishes, we would not suffer
not, say what virtue would consist of, ideal that everyone should strive
to reach, if your tongue is made like that of other men.

--Where am I? Have I not changed my character? I feel a breath
mighty consolation touch my reassured forehead like the breeze of the
spring revives the hope of the elderly. Who is this man whose
sublime language said things that the first comer would not have
pronounced? What a beauty of music in the incomparable melody of her
voice! I prefer to hear it speak, than sing others. However,
the more I observe it, the more its face is not blunt. The expression
general of its features contrasts singularly with these words that
the love of God alone could inspire. His forehead, wrinkled with a few folds,
is marked with an indelible stygma. This stygma, who aged him before
l'âge, est-il honorable ou est-il infâme? Ses rides doivent-elles être
regardées avec vénération? Je l'ignore et je crains de le savoir.
Quoiqu'il dise ce qu'il ne pense pas, je crois néanmoins qu'il a des
raisons pour agir comme il l'a fait, excité par les restes en lambeaux
d'une charité détruite en lui. Il est absorbé dans des méditations qui
me sont inconnues, et il redouble d'activité dans un travail ardu qu'il
n'a pas l'habitude d'entreprendre. La sueur mouille sa peau: il ne s'en
aperçoit pas. Il est plus triste que les sentiments qu'inspire la vue
d'un enfant au berceau. Oh! comme il est sombre!... D'où sors-tu?...
Étranger, permets que je touche, et que mes mains, qui étreignent
rarement celles des vivants, s'imposent sur la noblesse de ton corps.
Quoi qu'il en arrive, je saurais à quoi m'en tenir. Ces cheveux sont les
plus beaux que j'aie touchés dans ma vie. Qui serait assez audacieux
pour contester que je ne connais pas la qualité des cheveux?

--Que me veux-tu, quand je creuse une tombe? Le lion ne souhaite pas
qu'on l'agace, quand il se repaît. Si tu ne le sais pas, je te
l'apprends. Allons, dépêche-toi; accomplis ce que tu désires.

--Ce qui frissonne à mon contact, en me faisant frissonner moi-même, est
de la chair, à n'en pas douter. Il est vrai ... je ne rêve pas! Qui
es-tu donc, toi, qui te penches là pour creuser une tombe, tandis que,
comme un paresseux qui mange le pain des autres, je ne fais rien? C'est
l'heure de dormir, ou de sacrifier son repos à la science. En tout cas,
no one is absent from his house, and is careful not to leave the door open,
so as not to let thieves in. He locks himself in his room, the
best he can, while the ashes of the old chimney know
further warm the room from a remnant of heat. You don't
like the others; your clothes indicate a resident of some country
distant.

--While I am not tired, it is useless to dig the pit
more. Now undress me; then put me in it.

--The conversation, which we both have, for a few
moments, is so strange, that I do not know how to answer you ... I believe
that he wants to laugh.

--Yes, yes, it's true, I wanted to laugh; pay no more attention to what
I said.

He collapsed, and the gravedigger hastened to support him!

--What have you?

--Yes, yes, that's right, I lied ... I was tired when I
abandoned the pick ... this is the first time I have undertaken this
work ... no longer pay attention to what I said.

--My opinion takes more and more consistency: it's someone
who has appalling sorrows. Heaven take away the thought of
question him. I prefer to remain in uncertainty, as he inspires me to
pity. Then he wouldn't want to answer me, that's for sure: it's
suffer twice than to communicate his heart in this abnormal state.

- Let me out of this cemetery; I will continue my journey.

--Your legs do not support you; you would get lost while you
would walk. My duty is to offer you a coarse bed; I do not have any
else. Trust me; for hospitality will not demand
violation of your secrets.

--O venerable louse, you whose body is devoid of elytra, one day,
you bitterly reproach me for not loving your sublime enough
intelligence, which cannot be read: perhaps you were right,
since I don't even feel gratitude for this one. Lantern
from Maldoror, where do you guide his steps?

--Home. That you are a criminal, who did not have the precaution to
wash his right hand, with soap, after committing his crime, and
facile à reconnaître, par l'inspection de cette main; ou un frère qui a
perdu sa soeur; ou quelque monarque dépossédé, fuyant de ses royaumes,
mon palais vraiment grandiose, est digne de te recevoir. Il n'a pas été
built with diamond and precious stones, because it's only one
poor cottage, badly built; but, this famous thatched cottage has a past
history that the present constantly renews and continues. If she
could speak, she would surprise you, you, who seem to me not to surprise you
nothing. How many times, at the same time as she, have I seen parading before me
funeral beers, containing bones soon wormier than the
back of my door, against which I leaned. My countless
subjects are increasing every day. I don't need to do, at
fixed periods, no census to notice. Here it’s like
in the living; each pays a tax, proportional to the wealth of
the house he chose for himself; and, if some miser refused to
délivrer sa quote-part, j'ai ordre, en parlant à sa personne, de faire
comme les huissiers: il ne manque pas de chacals et de vautours qui
désireraient faire un bon repas. J'ai vu se ranger, sous les drapeaux de
la mort, celui qui fut beau; celui qui, après sa vie, n'a pas enlaidi;
l'homme, la femme, le mendiant, les fils de rois; les illusions de la
jeunesse, les squelettes des vieillards; le génie, la folie; la paresse,
son contraire; celui qui fut faux, celui qui fut vrai; le masque de
l'orgueilleux, la modestie de l'humble; le vice couronné de fleurs et
l'innocence trahie.

--Non certes, je ne refuse pas ta couche, qui est digne de moi, jusqu'à
ce que l'aurore vienne, qui ne tardera point. Je te remercie de ta
bienveillance ... Fossoyeur, il est beau de contempler les ruines des
cités; mais, il est plus beau de contempler les ruines des humains!

       *       *       *       *       *

Le frère de la sangsue marchait à pas lents dans la forêt. Il s'arrête à
plusieurs reprises, en ouvrant la bouche pour parler. Mais, chaque fois
sa gorge se resserre, et refoule en arrière l'effort avorté. Enfin, il
s'écrie: «Homme, lorsque tu rencontres un chien mort retourné, appuyé
contre une écluse qui l'empêche de partir, n'aille pas, comme les
autres, prendre avec ta main, les vers qui sortent de son ventre gonflé,
les considérer avec étonnement, ouvrir un couteau, puis en dépecer un
grand nombre, en te disant que, toi, aussi, tu ne seras pas plus que ce
chien. Quel mystère cherches-tu? Ni moi, ni les quatre pattes-nageoires
de l'ours marin de l'océan Boréal, n'avons pu trouver le problème de la
vie. Prends garde, la nuit s'approche, et tu es là depuis le matin. Que
dira ta famille, avec ta petite soeur, de te voir si tard arriver? Lave
tes mains, reprends la route qui va où tu dors ... Quel est cet être,
là-bas, à l'horizon, et qui ose approcher de moi, sans peur, à sauts
obliques et tourmentés; et quelle majesté, mêlée d'une douceur sereine!
Son regard, quoique doux, est profond. Ses paupières énormes jouent avec
la brise, et paraissent vivre. Il m'est inconnu. En fixant ses yeux
monstrueux, mon corps tremble; c'est la première fois, depuis que j'ai
sucé les sèches mamelles de ce qu'on appelle une mère. Il y a comme une
auréole de lumière éblouissante autour de lui. Quand il a parlé, tout
s'est tu dans la nature, et a éprouvé un grand frisson. Puisqu'il te
please come to me, as if attracted by a magnet, I will not oppose it
not. How handsome he is! It pains me to say it. You must be
powerful; because, you have a more than human figure, sad like the universe,
beautiful like suicide. I abhor you as much as I can; and I
prefer to see a snake, intertwined around my neck from the
beginning of centuries, that not your eyes ... How! ... it is
you, toad! ... big toad! ... unfortunate toad! ... Forgive! ...
forgive! ... What are you doing on this earth where the accursed are?
But what did you do with your slimy, foul pustules to
look so sweet? When you come down from above, by an order
superior, with the mission of consoling the various races of beings
existing, you fall on the earth, with the speed of Milan, the
wings not tired from this long, magnificent race; I live you!
Poor toad! Like then I thought of infinity, at the same time as
my weakness. "One more that is superior to those on earth, me
I said: that, by divine will. Why not too? What
good injustice, in the supreme decrees? Is it foolish, the Creator;
however the strongest, whose anger is terrible! ” Since you are me
appeared, monarch of ponds and swamps! covered with a glory which
belongs only to God, you have partly consoled me; but, my reason
tottering sinks before so much grandeur! Who are you then? Rest ...
Oh! still stay on this earth! Flip up your white wings, and don't
regarde pas en haut, avec des paupières inquiètes ... Si tu pars,
partons ensemble!» Le crapaud s'assit sur les cuisses de derrière (qui
ressemblent tant à celles de l'homme!) et, pendant que les limaces, les
cloportes et les limaçons s'enfuyaient à la vue de leur ennemi mortel,
prit la parole en ces termes: «Maldoror, écoute-moi. Remarque ma figure,
calme comme un miroir, et je crois avoir une intelligence égale à la
tienne. Un jour, tu m'appelas le soutien de ta vie. Depuis lors, je n'ai
pas démenti la confiance que tu m'avais vouée. Je ne suis qu'un simple
habitant des roseaux, c'est vrai; mais, grâce à ton propre contact, ne
prenant que ce qu'il y avait de beau en toi, ma raison s'est agrandie,
et je puis te parler. Je suis venu vers toi, afin de te retirer de
the abyss. Those who call themselves your friends look at you, struck with
dismay, every time they meet you, pale and hunched, in
theaters, in public places, in churches, or pressing,
two nervous thighs, this horse that gallops only at night,
while he is carrying his ghost master, wrapped in a long coat
black. Give up those thoughts, which make your heart empty like a desert;
they are hotter than fire. Your mind is so sick
that you do not notice it, and that you believe to be in your naturalness,
every time he makes foolish words out of your mouth, though
full of hellish grandeur. Unfortunate! what have you said since
day of your birth? O sad remains of an immortal intelligence, that
God had created with so much love! You only spawned curses
more frightful than the sight of hungry panthers! I would prefer to have
my eyelids stuck, my body missing legs and arms, having
murdered a man, what not to be you! Because I hate you. Why
have this character that surprises me? What right do you come from on this earth,
to mock those who inhabit it, rotten wreckage, tossed by
skepticism? If you don't like it, you have to go back to the spheres
where are you from. A resident of the cities must not reside in the villages,
like a stranger. We know that in spaces there are
spheres larger than ours, and whose minds have a
intelligence that we cannot even conceive of. Well, go! ...
withdraw from this mobile soil! ... finally show your divine essence, which you have
hidden so far; and, as soon as possible, direct your upward flight to
your sphere, that we do not envy, proud that you are! because, I am not
failed to recognize if you are a man or more than a man! Farewell
so; no longer hope to find the toad in your path. You were there
because of my death. I am leaving for eternity, to implore your forgiveness! ”

       * * * * *

If it sometimes makes sense to refer to the appearance of
phenomena, this first song ends here. Don't be harsh on that
who is still just trying his lyre: it makes such a strange sound!
However, if you want to be impartial, you will already recognize a
strong imprint, in the midst of imperfections. As for me, I will
put back to work, to make a second song appear, in a lapse
of time that is not too delayed. The end of the nineteenth century
